If the value changes,\n    39→\t// the transformer may report the value as unreadable or tampered. This may be nil if no such description exists\n    40→\t// or is needed. For additional verification, set this to data that strongly identifies the value, such as\n    41→\t// the key and creation version of the stored data.\n    42→\tAuthenticatedData() []byte\n    43→}\n    44→\n    45→type Read interface {\n    46→\t// TransformFromStorage may transform the provided data from its underlying storage representation or return an error.\n    47→\t// Stale is true if the object on disk is stale and a write to etcd should be issued, even if the contents of the object\n    48→\t// have not changed.\n    49→\tTransformFromStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, stale bool, err error)\n    50→}\n    51→\n    52→type Write interface {\n    53→\t// TransformToStorage may transform the provided data into the appropriate form in storage or return an error.\n    54→\tTransformToStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, err error)\n    55→}\n    56→\n    57→// Transformer allows a value to be transformed before being read from or written to the underlying store. The methods\n    58→// must be able to undo the transformation caused by the other.\n    59→type Transformer interface {\n    60→\tRead\n    61→\tWrite\n    62→}\n    63→\n    64→// ResourceTransformers returns a transformer for the provided resource.\n    65→type ResourceTransformers interface {\n    66→\tTransformerForResource(resource schema.GroupResource) Transformer\n    67→}\n    68→\n    69→// DefaultContext is a simple implementation of Context for a slice of bytes.\n    70→type DefaultContext []byte\n    71→\n    72→// AuthenticatedData returns itself.\n    73→func (c DefaultContext) AuthenticatedData() []byte { return c }\n    74→\n    75→// PrefixTransformer holds a transformer interface and the prefix that the transformation is located under.\n    76→type PrefixTransformer struct {\n    77→\tPrefix      []byte\n    78→\tTransformer Transformer\n    79→}\n    80→\n    81→type prefixTransformers struct {\n    82→\ttransformers []PrefixTransformer\n    83→\terr          error\n    84→}\n    85→\n    86→var _ Transformer = &prefixTransformers{}\n    87→\n    88→// NewPrefixTransformers supports the Transformer interface by checking the incoming data against the provided\n    89→// prefixes in order. The first matching prefix will be used to transform the value (the prefix is stripped\n    90→// before the Transformer interface is invoked). The first provided transformer will be used when writing to\n    91→// the store.\n    92→func NewPrefixTransformers(err error, transformers ...PrefixTransformer) Transformer {\n    93→\tif err == nil {\n    94→\t\terr = fmt.Errorf(\"the provided value does not match any of the supported transformers\")\n    95→\t}\n    96→\treturn &prefixTransformers{\n    97→\t\ttransformers: transformers,\n    98→\t\terr:          err,\n    99→\t}\n   100→}\n   101→\n   102→// TransformFromStorage finds the first transformer with a prefix matching the provided data and returns\n   103→// the result of transforming the value. It will always mark any transformation as stale that is not using\n   104→// the first transformer.\n   105→func (t *prefixTransformers) TransformFromStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) ([]byte, bool, error) {\n   106→\tstart := time.Now()\n   107→\tvar errs []error\n   108→\tresource := getResourceFromContext(ctx)\n   109→\tfor i, transformer := range t.transformers {\n   110→\t\tif bytes.HasPrefix(data, transformer.Prefix) {\n   111→\t\t\tresult, stale, err := transformer.Transformer.TransformFromStorage(ctx, data[len(transformer.Prefix):], dataCtx)\n   112→\t\t\t// To migrate away from encryption, user can specify an identity transformer higher up\n   113→\t\t\t// (in the config file) than the encryption transformer. In that scenario, the identity transformer needs to\n   114→\t\t\t// identify (during reads from disk) whether the data being read is encrypted or not. If the data is encrypted,\n   115→\t\t\t// it shall throw an error, but that error should not prevent the next subsequent transformer from being tried.\n   116→\t\t\tif len(transformer.Prefix) == 0 && err != nil {\n   117→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   118→\t\t\t}\n   119→\t\t\tif len(transformer.Prefix) == 0 {\n   120→\t\t\t\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", \"identity\", time.Since(start), err)\n   121→\t\t\t} else {\n   122→\t\t\t\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", string(transformer.Prefix), time.Since(start), err)\n   123→\t\t\t}\n   124→\n   125→\t\t\t// It is valid to have overlapping prefixes when the same encryption provider\n   126→\t\t\t// is specified multiple times but with different keys (the first provider is\n   127→\t\t\t// being rotated to and some later provider is being rotated away from).\n   128→\t\t\t//\n   129→\t\t\t// Example:\n   130→\t\t\t//\n   131→\t\t\t//  {\n   132→\t\t\t//    \"aescbc\": {\n   133→\t\t\t//      \"keys\": [\n   134→\t\t\t//        {\n   135→\t\t\t//          \"name\": \"2\",\n   136→\t\t\t//          \"secret\": \"some key 2\"\n   137→\t\t\t//        }\n   138→\t\t\t//      ]\n   139→\t\t\t//    }\n   140→\t\t\t//  },\n   141→\t\t\t//  {\n   142→\t\t\t//    \"aescbc\": {\n   143→\t\t\t//      \"keys\": [\n   144→\t\t\t//        {\n   145→\t\t\t//          \"name\": \"1\",\n   146→\t\t\t//          \"secret\": \"some key 1\"\n   147→\t\t\t//        }\n   148→\t\t\t//      ]\n   149→\t\t\t//    }\n   150→\t\t\t//  },\n   151→\t\t\t//\n   152→\t\t\t// The transformers for both aescbc configs share the prefix k8s:enc:aescbc:v1:\n   153→\t\t\t// but a failure in the first one should not prevent a later match from being attempted.\n   154→\t\t\t// Thus we never short-circuit on a prefix match that results in an error.\n   155→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   156→\t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n   157→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   158→\t\t\t}\n   159→\n   160→\t\t\treturn result, stale || i != 0, err\n   161→\t\t}\n   162→\t}\n   163→\tif err := errors.Reduce(errors.NewAggregate(errs)); err != nil {\n   164→\t\tlogTransformErr(ctx, err, \"failed to decrypt data\")\n   165→\t\treturn nil, false, err\n   166→\t}\n   167→\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", \"unknown\", time.Since(start), t.err)\n   168→\treturn nil, false, t.err\n   169→}\n   170→\n   171→// TransformToStorage uses the first transformer and adds its prefix to the data.\n   172→func (t *prefixTransformers) TransformToStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) ([]byte, error) {\n   173→\tstart := time.Now()\n   174→\ttransformer := t.transformers[0]\n   175→\tresource := getResourceFromContext(ctx)\n   176→\tresult, err := transformer.Transformer.TransformToStorage(ctx, data, dataCtx)\n   177→\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"to_storage\", string(transformer.Prefix), time.Since(start), err)\n   178→\tif err != nil {\n   179→\t\tlogTransformErr(ctx, err, \"failed to encrypt data\")\n   180→\t\treturn nil, err\n   181→\t}\n   182→\tprefixedData := make([]byte, len(transformer.Prefix), len(result)+len(transformer.Prefix))\n   183→\tcopy(prefixedData, transformer.Prefix)\n   184→\tprefixedData = append(prefixedData, result...)\n   185→\treturn prefixedData, nil\n   186→}\n   187→\n   188→func logTransformErr(ctx context.Context, err error, message string) {\n   189→\trequestInfo := getRequestInfoFromContext(ctx)\n   190→\tif klogLevel6 := klog.V(6); klogLevel6.Enabled() {\n   191→\t\tklogLevel6.InfoSDepth(\n   192→\t\t\t1,\n   193→\t\t\tmessage,\n 202→\t\t)\n   203→\n   204→\t\treturn\n   205→\t}\n   206→\n   207→\tklog.ErrorSDepth(1, err, message)\n   208→}\n   209→\n   210→func getRequestInfoFromContext(ctx context.Context) If the value changes,\n\t// the transformer may report the value as unreadable or tampered. This may be nil if no such description exists\n\t// or is needed. For additional verification, set this to data that strongly identifies the value, such as\n\t// the key and creation version of the stored data.\n\tAuthenticatedData() []byte\n}\n\ntype Read interface {\n\t// TransformFromStorage may transform the provided data from its underlying storage representation or return an error.\n\t// Stale is true if the object on disk is stale and a write to etcd should be issued, even if the contents of the object\n\t// have not changed.\n\tTransformFromStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, stale bool, err error)\n}\n\ntype Write interface {\n\t// TransformToStorage may transform the provided data into the appropriate form in storage or return an error.\n\tTransformToStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) (out []byte, err error)\n}\n\n// Transformer allows a value to be transformed before being read from or written to the underlying store. The methods\n// must be able to undo the transformation caused by the other.\ntype Transformer interface {\n\tRead\n\tWrite\n}\n\n// ResourceTransformers returns a transformer for the provided resource.\ntype ResourceTransformers interface {\n\tTransformerForResource(resource schema.GroupResource) Transformer\n}\n\n// DefaultContext is a simple implementation of Context for a slice of bytes.\ntype DefaultContext []byte\n\n// AuthenticatedData returns itself.\nfunc (c DefaultContext) AuthenticatedData() []byte { return c }\n\n// PrefixTransformer holds a transformer interface and the prefix that the transformation is located under.\ntype PrefixTransformer struct {\n\tPrefix      []byte\n\tTransformer Transformer\n}\n\ntype prefixTransformers struct {\n\ttransformers []PrefixTransformer\n\terr          error\n}\n\nvar _ Transformer = &prefixTransformers{}\n\n// NewPrefixTransformers supports the Transformer interface by checking the incoming data against the provided\n// prefixes in order. The first matching prefix will be used to transform the value (the prefix is stripped\n// before the Transformer interface is invoked). The first provided transformer will be used when writing to\n// the store.\nfunc NewPrefixTransformers(err error, transformers ...PrefixTransformer) Transformer {\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\terr = fmt.Errorf(\"the provided value does not match any of the supported transformers\")\n\t}\n\treturn &prefixTransformers{\n\t\ttransformers: transformers,\n\t\terr:          err,\n\t}\n}\n\n// TransformFromStorage finds the first transformer with a prefix matching the provided data and returns\n// the result of transforming the value. It will always mark any transformation as stale that is not using\n// the first transformer.\nfunc (t *prefixTransformers) TransformFromStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) ([]byte, bool, error) {\n\tstart := time.Now()\n\tvar errs []error\n\tresource := getResourceFromContext(ctx)\n\tfor i, transformer := range t.transformers {\n\t\tif bytes.HasPrefix(data, transformer.Prefix) {\n\t\t\tresult, stale, err := transformer.Transformer.TransformFromStorage(ctx, data[len(transformer.Prefix):], dataCtx)\n\t\t\t// To migrate away from encryption, user can specify an identity transformer higher up\n\t\t\t// (in the config file) than the encryption transformer. In that scenario, the identity transformer needs to\n\t\t\t// identify (during reads from disk) whether the data being read is encrypted or not. If the data is encrypted,\n\t\t\t// it shall throw an error, but that error should not prevent the next subsequent transformer from being tried.\n\t\t\tif len(transformer.Prefix) == 0 && err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif len(transformer.Prefix) == 0 {\n\t\t\t\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", \"identity\", time.Since(start), err)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", string(transformer.Prefix), time.Since(start), err)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// It is valid to have overlapping prefixes when the same encryption provider\n\t\t\t// is specified multiple times but with different keys (the first provider is\n\t\t\t// being rotated to and some later provider is being rotated away from).\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// Example:\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t//  {\n\t\t\t//    \"aescbc\": {\n\t\t\t//      \"keys\": [\n\t\t\t//        {\n\t\t\t//          \"name\": \"2\",\n\t\t\t//          \"secret\": \"some key 2\"\n\t\t\t//        }\n\t\t\t//      ]\n\t\t\t//    }\n\t\t\t//  },\n\t\t\t//  {\n\t\t\t//    \"aescbc\": {\n\t\t\t//      \"keys\": [\n\t\t\t//        {\n\t\t\t//          \"name\": \"1\",\n\t\t\t//          \"secret\": \"some key 1\"\n\t\t\t//        }\n\t\t\t//      ]\n\t\t\t//    }\n\t\t\t//  },\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// The transformers for both aescbc configs share the prefix k8s:enc:aescbc:v1:\n\t\t\t// but a failure in the first one should not prevent a later match from being attempted.\n\t\t\t// Thus we never short-circuit on a prefix match that results in an error.\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\treturn result, stale || i != 0, err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif err := errors.Reduce(errors.NewAggregate(errs)); err != nil {\n\t\tlogTransformErr(ctx, err, \"failed to decrypt data\")\n\t\treturn nil, false, err\n\t}\n\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"from_storage\", \"unknown\", time.Since(start), t.err)\n\treturn nil, false, t.err\n}\n\n// TransformToStorage uses the first transformer and adds its prefix to the data.\nfunc (t *prefixTransformers) TransformToStorage(ctx context.Context, data []byte, dataCtx Context) ([]byte, error) {\n\tstart := time.Now()\n\ttransformer := t.transformers[0]\n\tresource := getResourceFromContext(ctx)\n\tresult, err := transformer.Transformer.TransformToStorage(ctx, data, dataCtx)\n\tRecordTransformation(resource, \"to_storage\", string(transformer.Prefix), time.Since(start), err)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tlogTransformErr(ctx, err, \"failed to encrypt data\")\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tprefixedData := make([]byte, len(transformer.Prefix), len(result)+len(transformer.Prefix))\n\tcopy(prefixedData, transformer.Prefix)\n\tprefixedData = append(prefixedData, result...)\n\treturn prefixedData, nil\n}\n\nfunc logTransformErr(ctx context.Context, err error, message string) {\n\trequestInfo := getRequestInfoFromContext(ctx)\n\tif klogLevel6 := klog.V(6); klogLevel6.Enabled() {\n\t\tklogLevel6.InfoSDepth(\n\t\t\t1,\n\t\t\tmessage,\n\t\t\t\"err\", err,\n\t\t\t\"group\", requestInfo.APIGroup,\n\t\t\t\"version\", requestInfo.APIVersion,\n\t\t\t\"resource\", requestInfo.Resource,\n\t\t\t\"subresource\", requestInfo.Subresource,\n\t\t\t\"verb\", requestInfo.Verb,\n\t\t\t\"namespace\", requestInfo.Namespace,\n\t\t\t\"name\", requestInfo.Name,\n\t\t)\n\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tklog.ErrorSDepth(1, err, message)\n}\n\nfunc getRequestInfoFromContext(ctx context.Context) *genericapirequest.RequestInfo {\n\tif reqInfo, found := genericapirequest.RequestInfoFrom(ctx); found {\n\t\treturn reqInfo\n\t}\n\tklog.V(4).InfoSDepth(1, \"no request info on context\")\n\treturn &genericapirequest.RequestInfo{}\n}\n\nfunc getResourceFromContext(ctx context.Context) string {\n\treqInfo := getRequestInfoFromContext(ctx)\n\treturn schema.GroupResource{Group: reqInfo.APIGroup, Resource: reqInfo.Resource}.String()\n}\n","numLines":222,"startLine":1,"totalLines":222}}}
